lets do the following - STEP 3 — DB Schema Alignment Pass

Because you now have workflows calling:

clients

credit_transactions

payouts

jobs

disputes

cleaners

payments

We will make sure:

every column used in queries actually exists

the inserts and updates match your real schema

missing tables get generated

missing columns get added

ENUM fields get standardized

timestamp naming is consistent (e.g., created_at, updated_at, paid_at, etc.)

Perfect, this is the right moment to do the schema pass. I’ll give you a single canonical SQL schema that:

Covers all tables your workflows reference

Makes sure every column we’ve used actually exists

Standardizes names (created_at, updated_at, etc.)

Sets you up nicely for credits / payouts / disputes / KPIs / backups

You can treat this as a “source of truth” migration and adapt it to Neon.

🧱 1. Enums (for cleaner, safer statuses)
-- Job status over lifecycle
DO $$ BEGIN
  CREATE TYPE job_status_enum AS ENUM (
    'draft',
    'scheduled',
    'in_progress',
    'completed',
    'cancelled_by_client',
    'cancelled_by_cleaner',
    'no_show_by_client',
    'no_show_by_cleaner'
  );
EXCEPTION
  WHEN duplicate_object THEN NULL;
END $$;

-- Dispute status
DO $$ BEGIN
  CREATE TYPE dispute_status_enum AS ENUM (
    'open',
    'won',
    'lost'
  );
EXCEPTION
  WHEN duplicate_object THEN NULL;
END $$;

-- Payout status
DO $$ BEGIN
  CREATE TYPE payout_status_enum AS ENUM (
    'pending',
    'processing',
    'paid',
    'failed'
  );
EXCEPTION
  WHEN duplicate_object THEN NULL;
END $$;
👤 2. Clients
Used in: 03, 04, 05, 06, 11 (KPI), etc.

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS clients (
  id                    BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  stripe_customer_id    TEXT UNIQUE,
  email                 TEXT UNIQUE,
  phone                 TEXT,
  first_name            TEXT,
  last_name             TEXT,
  credit_balance        NUMERIC(12,2) NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,  -- credits in your system
  created_at            TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
  updated_at            TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);

-- Helpful index
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_clients_stripe_customer
  ON clients (stripe_customer_id);
🧹 3. Cleaners
Used in: payouts, reliability, payout failures (08, 09), KPIs.

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS cleaners (
  id                         BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  stripe_account_id          TEXT UNIQUE,      -- Stripe Connect account
  email                      TEXT,
  phone                      TEXT,
  first_name                 TEXT,
  last_name                  TEXT,
  tier                       TEXT,            -- e.g. 'bronze', 'silver', 'gold'
  reliability_score          NUMERIC(5,2) DEFAULT 100,  -- 0–100
  lifetime_earnings_cents    BIGINT NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  last_payout_at             TIMESTAMPTZ,
  has_payout_issue           BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT FALSE,
  last_payout_issue_at       TIMESTAMPTZ,
  created_at                 TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
  updated_at                 TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);
🧾 4. Jobs
Used in: 06, 07, 10, 11.

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS jobs (
  id                 BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  client_id          BIGINT NOT NULL REFERENCES clients(id),
  cleaner_id         BIGINT REFERENCES cleaners(id),
  status             job_status_enum NOT NULL DEFAULT 'draft',
  dispute_status     dispute_status_enum DEFAULT NULL,   -- null or 'open'/'won'/'lost'
  scheduled_start_at TIMESTAMPTZ,
  scheduled_end_at   TIMESTAMPTZ,
  check_in_at        TIMESTAMPTZ,
  check_out_at       TIMESTAMPTZ,
  completed_at       TIMESTAMPTZ,
  cancelled_at       TIMESTAMPTZ,
  base_price_cents   BIGINT,
  notes              TEXT,
  created_at         TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
  updated_at         TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_jobs_client_id ON jobs (client_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_jobs_cleaner_id ON jobs (cleaner_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_jobs_status ON jobs (status);
💳 5. Payments
Used in: 05 (refund context), 06 (dispute join), 11 (KPI revenue).

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS payments (
  id                        BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  client_id                 BIGINT NOT NULL REFERENCES clients(id),
  job_id                    BIGINT REFERENCES jobs(id),
  stripe_payment_intent_id  TEXT,
  stripe_charge_id          TEXT,
  amount_cents              BIGINT NOT NULL,
  currency                  TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'usd',
  status                    TEXT,                  -- e.g. 'succeeded', 'failed', 'refunded'
  created_at                TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
  updated_at                TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_payments_pi ON payments (stripe_payment_intent_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_payments_charge ON payments (stripe_charge_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_payments_client ON payments (client_id);
🪙 6. Credit Transactions
Used heavily in: 03, 05, 11.

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS credit_transactions (
  id                     BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  client_id              BIGINT NOT NULL REFERENCES clients(id),
  stripe_payment_intent_id TEXT,
  stripe_charge_id       TEXT,
  stripe_event_id        TEXT,
  credit_change          NUMERIC(12,2) NOT NULL,     -- positive or negative
  credit_source          TEXT NOT NULL,              -- 'stripe_payment', 'stripe_credit_refund', 'job_charge', etc.
  related_credit_tx_id   BIGINT REFERENCES credit_transactions(id),
  metadata               JSONB,
  created_at             TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_credit_tx_client ON credit_transactions (client_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_credit_tx_event ON credit_transactions (stripe_event_id);
In workflow queries, we sometimes called columns like credits_change or credit_change; this schema standardizes on credit_change. We’ll adjust queries later to match.

💥 7. Payment Failures (from 04 – Payment Failed Processor)
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS payment_failures (
  id                          BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  client_id                   BIGINT REFERENCES clients(id),
  stripe_payment_intent_id    TEXT,
  stripe_event_id             TEXT,
  amount_cents                BIGINT,
  currency                    TEXT,
  failure_code                TEXT,
  failure_message             TEXT,
  raw_metadata                JSONB,
  created_at                  TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_payment_fail_pi ON payment_failures (stripe_payment_intent_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_payment_fail_client ON payment_failures (client_id);
💸 8. Payouts
Used in: 08 (paid), 09 (failed), 11 (KPI).

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS payouts (
  id                      BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  cleaner_id              BIGINT NOT NULL REFERENCES cleaners(id),
  stripe_payout_id        TEXT UNIQUE,
  total_amount_cents      BIGINT NOT NULL,
  currency                TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'usd',
  status                  payout_status_enum NOT NULL DEFAULT 'pending',
  payout_batch_id         TEXT,                  -- optional grouping
  stripe_event_id_paid    TEXT,
  stripe_event_id_failed  TEXT,
  arrival_date            TIMESTAMPTZ,
  paid_at                 TIMESTAMPTZ,
  failed_at               TIMESTAMPTZ,
  failure_code            TEXT,
  failure_message         TEXT,
  created_at              TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
  updated_at              TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_payouts_cleaner ON payouts (cleaner_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_payouts_status ON payouts (status);
⚖️ 9. Disputes
Used in: 06 (created), 07 (closed).

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS disputes (
  id                          BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  stripe_dispute_id           TEXT UNIQUE,
  stripe_charge_id            TEXT,
  stripe_payment_intent_id    TEXT,
  stripe_event_id             TEXT,
  client_id                   BIGINT REFERENCES clients(id),
  job_id                      BIGINT REFERENCES jobs(id),
  cleaner_id                  BIGINT REFERENCES cleaners(id),
  amount_cents                BIGINT,
  currency                    TEXT,
  reason                      TEXT,
  status                      dispute_status_enum NOT NULL DEFAULT 'open',
  raw_metadata                JSONB,
  raw_evidence                JSONB,
  created_at                  TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
  closed_at                   TIMESTAMPTZ
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_disputes_charge ON disputes (stripe_charge_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_disputes_pi ON disputes (stripe_payment_intent_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_disputes_client ON disputes (client_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_disputes_job ON disputes (job_id);
📊 10. KPI Daily
Used in: 11 – KPI & Reporting Aggregator.

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS kpi_daily (
  id                    BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  date                  DATE NOT NULL UNIQUE,
  total_credits_sold    NUMERIC(14,2) NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  total_credits_used    NUMERIC(14,2) NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  total_revenue_cents   BIGINT NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  total_payouts_cents   BIGINT NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  jobs_created          INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  jobs_completed        INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  new_clients           INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  new_cleaners          INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  created_at            TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);
💾 11. Backup Runs
Used in: 12 – Daily Backup & Snapshot.

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS backup_runs (
  id         BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  run_at     TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
  status     TEXT NOT NULL,     -- 'started', 'success', 'failed', etc.
  notes      TEXT
);
🧹 12. Helpful “updated_at” trigger (optional)
If you want updated_at to auto-update on any row change:

CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION set_updated_at()
RETURNS TRIGGER AS $$
BEGIN
  NEW.updated_at = NOW();
  RETURN NEW;
END;
$$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;

-- Attach this trigger to tables that have updated_at:
DO $$ BEGIN
  CREATE TRIGGER set_timestamp_clients
  BEFORE UPDATE ON clients
  FOR EACH ROW
  EXECUTE PROCEDURE set_updated_at();
EXCEPTION WHEN duplicate_object THEN NULL; END $$;

DO $$ BEGIN
  CREATE TRIGGER set_timestamp_cleaners
  BEFORE UPDATE ON cleaners
  FOR EACH ROW
  EXECUTE PROCEDURE set_updated_at();
EXCEPTION WHEN duplicate_object THEN NULL; END $$;

DO $$ BEGIN
  CREATE TRIGGER set_timestamp_jobs
  BEFORE UPDATE ON jobs
  FOR EACH ROW
  EXECUTE PROCEDURE set_updated_at();
EXCEPTION WHEN duplicate_object THEN NULL; END $$;

DO $$ BEGIN
  CREATE TRIGGER set_timestamp_payments
  BEFORE UPDATE ON payments
  FOR EACH ROW
  EXECUTE PROCEDURE set_updated_at();
EXCEPTION WHEN duplicate_object THEN NULL; END $$;

DO $$ BEGIN
  CREATE TRIGGER set_timestamp_payouts
  BEFORE UPDATE ON payouts
  FOR EACH ROW
  EXECUTE PROCEDURE set_updated_at();
EXCEPTION WHEN duplicate_object THEN NULL; END $$;

✅ CHOOSE ONE FORMAT
Option A — “Database Schema JSON” (Recommended)
This is a JSON object that fully describes your database, like this structure:

{

    "clients": {
      "columns": { ... },
      "indexes": [ ... ]
    },
    "credit_transactions": { ... },
    "payouts": { ... },
    ...
  },
  "enums": {
    "job_status_enum": [ ... ],
    "dispute_status_enum": [ ... ],
    "payout_status_enum": [ ... ]
  }
}
✔️ Best for documentation
✔️ Perfect for AI
✔️ Easily readable
✔️ Matches your workflows
✔️ Can be imported into tools

Option B — “Neon Migration JSON”
This format generates JSON that tools like migration engines use:

{
  "migrations": [
    {
      "id": "001_init",
      "sql": "CREATE TABLE clients ( ... );"
    },
    {
      "id": "002_enums",
      "sql": "CREATE TYPE job_status_enum ..."
    }
  ]
}
✔️ Good for version-control
✔️ Good for manual DB management

Option C — “n8n Workflow Import JSON”
This JSON contains all workflows 1–12 bundled together so you can import them into n8n in one click.

(This is NOT what you asked for, but if you want it, I can generate it too.)

📦 PureTask Database Schema – Single JSON
You can copy–paste this, save it as puretask_schema.json, and reuse it anywhere.

{
  "enums": {
    "job_status_enum": [
      "draft",
      "scheduled",
      "in_progress",
      "completed",
      "cancelled_by_client",
      "cancelled_by_cleaner",
      "no_show_by_client",
      "no_show_by_cleaner"
    ],
    "dispute_status_enum": [
      "open",
      "won",
      "lost"
    ],
    "payout_status_enum": [
      "pending",
      "processing",
      "paid",
      "failed"
    ]
  },
  "tables": {
    "clients": {
      "description": "End customers who buy credits and book cleanings.",
      "columns": {
        "id": {
          "type": "bigserial",
          "primary_key": true,
          "nullable": false
        },
        "stripe_customer_id": {
          "type": "text",
          "unique": true,
          "nullable": true
        },
        "email": {
          "type": "text",
          "unique": true,
          "nullable": true
        },
        "phone": {
          "type": "text",
          "nullable": true"
        },
        "first_name": {
          "type": "text",
          "nullable": true
        },
        "last_name": {
          "type": "text",
          "nullable": true
        },
        "credit_balance": {
          "type": "numeric(12,2)",
          "nullable": false,
          "default": 0,
          "description": "Current available credits for this client"
        },
        "created_at": {
          "type": "timestamptz",
          "nullable": false,
          "default": "NOW()"
        },
        "updated_at": {
          "type": "timestamptz",
          "nullable": false,
          "default": "NOW()"
        }
      },
      "indexes": [
        {
          "name": "idx_clients_stripe_customer",
          "columns": ["stripe_customer_id"]
        }
      ]
    },
    "cleaners": {
      "description": "Service providers (cleaners) on the platform.",
      "columns": {
        "id": {
          "type": "bigserial",
          "primary_key": true,

DO WE NEED TO BOOT UP THE SERVER AND STUFF?

No — you do NOT need to “boot up a server” or run anything extra.

✔️ Your Neon Database Is Already Running
Neon is a serverless Postgres provider — that means:

There is no server for you to start

Your database is always running automatically

The SQL Editor in your screenshot executes queries directly on your production database

So the error you’re seeing has nothing to do with the server not running.

It simply means:

❌ You tried to run JSON in the SQL Editor
The bottom red error:

ERROR: syntax error at or near "{"
is because you pasted a JSON schema into a location that expects PostgreSQL SQL, not JSON.

The big red box in your screenshot is not SQL — it's JSON describing your schema.

✔️ To Fix This
1. You need real SQL, not JSON
PostgreSQL only accepts SQL in the SQL Editor:

CREATE TABLE ...

ALTER TABLE ... ADD COLUMN

CREATE TYPE ...

etc.

JSON schemas are for describing structure, not executing.

✔️ So What Do We Do Next?
Since you want:

“1 single JSON with ALL the DB schema, combined, that I can use for my workflows”

I can give you:

Option A: A full JSON schema (for documentation and n8n AI)
✔️ N8N AI loves JSON structure
✔️ Great for generating workflows
❌ Cannot be run in Postgres

Option B: A full SQL schema (to run inside Neon)
✔️ Actually creates tables
✔️ Actually adds columns
✔️ Actually builds ENUM types
❌ Not for n8n AI prompts

Option C (BEST): Both versions
One file for your database (SQL)
One file for your n8n system design (JSON)

💬 Before I generate them:
I need a quick confirmation from you:

❓ Do you want:
Option A — JSON only
(for n8n AI to read & help write workflows)

Option B — SQL only
(to run in Neon & physically build/update your schema)

Option C (recommended) — Both JSON + SQL
(one for n8n, one for your real database)

Which option do you choose?

OPTION C, LETS COVER THEM 1 AT A TIME

2️⃣ SQL schema (to run in Neon)
⚠️ Run this in your Neon SQL Editor (production branch) as SQL, not JSON.

-- 1. ENUM TYPES
-- Run this once. If you get "type already exists", it just means it was created before.

CREATE TYPE job_status_enum AS ENUM (
  'draft',
  'scheduled',
  'in_progress',
  'completed',
  'cancelled_by_client',
  'cancelled_by_cleaner',
  'no_show_by_client',
  'no_show_by_cleaner'
);

CREATE TYPE dispute_status_enum AS ENUM (
  'open',
  'won',
  'lost'
);

CREATE TYPE payout_status_enum AS ENUM (
  'pending',
  'processing',
  'paid',
  'failed'
);

CREATE TYPE credit_change_reason_enum AS ENUM (
  'booking_charge',
  'booking_refund',
  'cleaner_payout',
  'payout_reversal',
  'manual_adjustment',
  'signup_bonus',
  'promo_credit',
  'dispute_credit'
);

CREATE TYPE client_status_enum AS ENUM (
  'active',
  'paused',
  'banned'
);

-- 2. CLIENTS TABLE

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS clients (
  id                  uuid PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),
  stripe_customer_id  text UNIQUE,
  full_name           text,
  email               text NOT NULL UNIQUE,
  phone               text,
  status              client_status_enum NOT NULL DEFAULT 'active',
  credit_balance      integer NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  reliability_score   numeric(4,2),
  created_at          timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  updated_at          timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

-- 3. OPTIONAL: helpful indexes (redundant if UNIQUE already created them, but safe)

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_clients_stripe_customer_id
  ON clients (stripe_customer_id);
How to run this in Neon
Open Neon → SQL Editor (like in your screenshot).

Make sure branch = production (or whatever branch you want).

Paste the SQL block only (not the JSON) into the editor.

Click Run.

If you get errors like type "job_status_enum" already exists:

That means we already created that enum earlier.

You can comment that CREATE TYPE line out and re-run, or just ignore it if the rest ran.

✅ CHUNK 2 — CLEANERS
This chunk defines the cleaners table + all columns + enums + required indexes.

⭐ PART 1 — SQL VERSION (this is what you RUN in Neon)
👉 Copy + paste this entire block into Neon SQL editor and run it.

--
-- ENUM: cleaner_status_enum
-- Represents onboarding & availability state of a cleaner
--
DO $$ BEGIN
    CREATE TYPE cleaner_status_enum AS ENUM (
        'pending_verification',
        'active',
        'inactive',
        'suspended'
    );
EXCEPTION
    WHEN duplicate_object THEN null;
END $$;

--
-- CLEANERS TABLE
--

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS cleaners (
    id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),

    -- basic identity
    full_name TEXT NOT NULL,
    email TEXT UNIQUE NOT NULL,
    phone TEXT,

    -- onboarding & status
    status cleaner_status_enum NOT NULL DEFAULT 'pending_verification',
    background_check_complete BOOLEAN DEFAULT FALSE,

    -- payout info
    stripe_connected_account_id TEXT,
    payout_method TEXT,                     -- e.g. "bank_account", "paypal"
    payout_last_4 TEXT,

    -- business metrics
    rating NUMERIC(3,2) DEFAULT 5.00,
    total_jobs_completed INT DEFAULT 0,
    total_earnings_cents BIGINT DEFAULT 0,

    -- misc
    notes TEXT,

    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW(),
    updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW()
);

--
-- AUTOMATIC TIMESTAMP UPDATES
--
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION update_cleaners_updated_at()
RETURNS TRIGGER AS $$
BEGIN
    NEW.updated_at = NOW();
    RETURN NEW;
END;
$$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;

DROP TRIGGER IF EXISTS tr_cleaners_updated ON cleaners;

CREATE TRIGGER tr_cleaners_updated
    BEFORE UPDATE ON cleaners
    FOR EACH ROW EXECUTE FUNCTION update_cleaners_updated_at();

--
-- INDEXES
--
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_cleaners_email ON cleaners(email);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_cleaners_status ON cleaners(status);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_cleaners_stripe_account ON cleaners(stripe_connected_account_id);

👉 Save it in Notion/Google Docs as chunk-2-cleaners.json.

    "phone": { "type": "text", "nullable": true },

🧱 SQL BLOCK — Payments + Payment Events + Disputes
👉 Copy this entire thing into Neon SQL Editor and run it once.
(Like before, yellow “already exists, skipping” messages are fine.)

--
-- ENUMS (safe-creation)
--

DO $$ BEGIN
    CREATE TYPE payment_status_enum AS ENUM (
        'pending',
        'succeeded',
        'failed',
        'refunded',
        'partially_refunded'
    );
EXCEPTION
    WHEN duplicate_object THEN null;
END $$;

DO $$ BEGIN
    CREATE TYPE dispute_status_enum AS ENUM (
        'open',
        'needs_response',
        'under_review',
        'won',
        'lost',
        'cancelled'
    );
EXCEPTION
    WHEN duplicate_object THEN null;
END $$;

--
-- PAYMENTS TABLE
-- One row per Stripe PaymentIntent / Charge we care about.
--

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS payments (
    id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),

    -- Foreign keys
    client_id UUID REFERENCES clients(id),

    -- Stripe references
    stripe_payment_intent_id TEXT UNIQUE,
    stripe_charge_id TEXT,
    stripe_refund_id TEXT,

    -- Money
    amount_cents BIGINT NOT NULL,
    currency TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'usd',

    -- Status and type
    status payment_status_enum NOT NULL DEFAULT 'pending',
    payment_method TEXT,                  -- e.g. "card", "bank_account"
    is_test BOOLEAN DEFAULT TRUE,         -- true for sandbox/test transactions

    -- Metadata & notes
    description TEXT,
    metadata JSONB,

    -- Important timestamps
    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW(),
    updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW(),
    captured_at TIMESTAMPTZ,
    refunded_at TIMESTAMPTZ
);

--
-- Automatic updated_at on payments
--
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION update_payments_updated_at()
RETURNS TRIGGER AS $$
BEGIN
    NEW.updated_at = NOW();
    RETURN NEW;
END;
$$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;

DROP TRIGGER IF EXISTS tr_payments_updated ON payments;

CREATE TRIGGER tr_payments_updated
    BEFORE UPDATE ON payments
    FOR EACH ROW EXECUTE FUNCTION update_payments_updated_at();

--
-- Indexes for payments
--
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_payments_client_id ON payments(client_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_payments_status ON payments(status);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_payments_stripe_pi ON payments(stripe_payment_intent_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_payments_stripe_charge ON payments(stripe_charge_id);


--
-- PAYMENT EVENTS TABLE
-- Raw Stripe webhook event log, linked to a payment when possible.
--

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS payment_events (
    id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),

    payment_id UUID REFERENCES payments(id) ON DELETE CASCADE,

    stripe_event_id TEXT UNIQUE,
    event_type TEXT NOT NULL,         -- e.g. "payment_intent.succeeded"
    api_version TEXT,
    livemode BOOLEAN,

    raw_event JSONB NOT NULL,

    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW()
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_payment_events_payment_id ON payment_events(payment_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_payment_events_event_type ON payment_events(event_type);


--
-- DISPUTES TABLE
-- Tracks chargebacks / disputes tied to a payment.
--

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS disputes (
    id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),

    payment_id UUID REFERENCES payments(id),
    client_id UUID REFERENCES clients(id),

    stripe_dispute_id TEXT UNIQUE,
    status dispute_status_enum NOT NULL DEFAULT 'open',

    amount_cents BIGINT,
    currency TEXT DEFAULT 'usd',

    reason TEXT,                     -- high-level dispute reason
    evidence JSONB,                  -- any structured evidence we store
    admin_notes TEXT,

    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW(),
    updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW(),
    closed_at TIMESTAMPTZ
);

--
-- Automatic updated_at on disputes
--
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION update_disputes_updated_at()
RETURNS TRIGGER AS $$
BEGIN
    NEW.updated_at = NOW();
    RETURN NEW;
END;
$$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;

DROP TRIGGER IF EXISTS tr_disputes_updated ON disputes;

CREATE TRIGGER tr_disputes_updated
    BEFORE UPDATE ON disputes
    FOR EACH ROW EXECUTE FUNCTION update_disputes_updated_at();

--
-- Indexes for disputes
--
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_disputes_payment_id ON disputes(payment_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_disputes_client_id ON disputes(client_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_disputes_status ON disputes(status);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_disputes_stripe_dispute_id ON disputes(stripe_dispute_id);
Run that once. If you see “already exists, skipping”, that’s fine.

🧱 CHUNK 3 — SQL
Tables: credit_transactions, payouts
Enums: credit_transaction_type_enum, payout_status_enum

👉 Copy–paste ALL of this into Neon SQL Editor (production branch) and run once.

--
-- ENUMS
--

DO $$ BEGIN
    CREATE TYPE credit_transaction_type_enum AS ENUM (
        'purchase',          -- client buys credits with Stripe
        'job_hold',          -- credits reserved/escrowed for a job
        'job_release',       -- credits released when job completes
        'job_refund',        -- credits returned to client (refund/discount)
        'admin_adjustment',  -- manual admin change
        'expiration'         -- credits expired
    );
EXCEPTION
    WHEN duplicate_object THEN null;
END $$;

DO $$ BEGIN
    CREATE TYPE payout_status_enum AS ENUM (
        'pending',           -- created, not sent to Stripe yet
        'processing',        -- sent to Stripe / in transit
        'paid',              -- successfully paid out
        'failed',            -- failed payout
        'canceled'           -- manually cancelled
    );
EXCEPTION
    WHEN duplicate_object THEN null;
END $$;


--
-- CREDIT TRANSACTIONS
-- Ledger for client credit balance movements.
--

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS credit_transactions (
    id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),

    client_id UUID NOT NULL REFERENCES clients(id),
    job_id UUID REFERENCES jobs(id),
    payment_id UUID REFERENCES payments(id),

    type credit_transaction_type_enum NOT NULL,

    -- Positive = client gains credits, negative = loses credits
    amount_credits NUMERIC(12,2) NOT NULL,
    balance_after_credits NUMERIC(12,2),  -- optional running balance snapshot

    -- Helpful references
    stripe_payment_intent_id TEXT,
    stripe_charge_id TEXT,

    description TEXT,
    metadata JSONB,

    created_by TEXT DEFAULT 'system',      -- 'system', 'admin', etc.
    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW()
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_credit_tx_client_id
    ON credit_transactions(client_id);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_credit_tx_job_id
    ON credit_transactions(job_id);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_credit_tx_payment_id
    ON credit_transactions(payment_id);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_credit_tx_type
    ON credit_transactions(type);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_credit_tx_created_at
    ON credit_transactions(created_at);


--
-- PAYOUTS
-- High-level payouts sent to cleaners (weekly or ad-hoc).
--

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS payouts (
    id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),

    cleaner_id UUID NOT NULL REFERENCES cleaners(id),

    -- Money
    amount_cents BIGINT NOT NULL,
    currency TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'usd',

    -- Status and Stripe references
    status payout_status_enum NOT NULL DEFAULT 'pending',
    stripe_payout_id TEXT,          -- Stripe Payout ID (balance → bank)
    stripe_transfer_group TEXT,     -- Optional transfer group / batch key

    -- Period this payout covers (for reporting)
    period_start DATE,
    period_end DATE,

    attempt_count INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
    failure_reason TEXT,
    metadata JSONB,

    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW(),
    updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW(),
    paid_at TIMESTAMPTZ
);

--
-- Automatic updated_at on payouts
--

CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION update_payouts_updated_at()
RETURNS TRIGGER AS $$
BEGIN
    NEW.updated_at = NOW();
    RETURN NEW;
END;
$$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;

DROP TRIGGER IF EXISTS tr_payouts_updated ON payouts;

CREATE TRIGGER tr_payouts_updated
    BEFORE UPDATE ON payouts
    FOR EACH ROW EXECUTE FUNCTION update_payouts_updated_at();


--
-- Indexes for payouts
--

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_payouts_cleaner_id
    ON payouts(cleaner_id);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_payouts_status
    ON payouts(status);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_payouts_period
    ON payouts(period_start, period_end);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_payouts_stripe_payout_id
    ON payouts(stripe_payout_id);
✅ As before, yellow “already exists, skipping” notices are OK.
We only care about red errors (if any).

📄 CHUNK 3 — JSON Blueprint (for n8n AI)
👉 Save this as something like:
schema-chunk-03-credit-transactions-payouts.json

Use it when talking to n8n AI so it writes queries that match your DB.

{
  "enums": {
    "credit_transaction_type_enum": [
      "purchase",
      "job_hold",
      "job_release",
      "job_refund",
      "admin_adjustment",
      "expiration"
    ],
    "payout_status_enum": [
      "pending",
      "processing",
      "paid",
      "failed",
      "canceled"
    ]
  },
  "tables": {
    "credit_transactions": {
      "description": "Ledger of all client credit movements (purchases, holds, releases, refunds, adjustments, expirations).",
      "columns": {
        "id": { "type": "uuid", "primary_key": true },
        "client_id": { "type": "uuid", "references": "clients.id", "nullable": false },
        "job_id": { "type": "uuid", "references": "jobs.id" },
        "payment_id": { "type": "uuid", "references": "payments.id" },

        "type": {
          "type": "credit_transaction_type_enum",
          "nullable": false
        },

        "amount_credits": {
          "type": "numeric(12,2)",
          "nullable": false,
          "description": "Positive = client gains credits; negative = client loses credits."
        },
        "balance_after_credits": {
          "type": "numeric(12,2)",
          "description": "Client credit balance immediately after this transaction."
        },

        "stripe_payment_intent_id": { "type": "text" },
        "stripe_charge_id": { "type": "text" },

        "description": { "type": "text" },
        "metadata": { "type": "jsonb" },

        "created_by": { "type": "text", "default": "system" },
        "created_at": { "type": "timestamptz", "default": "NOW()" }
      },
      "indexes": [
        "client_id",
        "job_id",
        "payment_id",
        "type",
        "created_at"
      ]
    },

    "payouts": {
      "description": "Records payouts sent (or scheduled) to cleaners via Stripe Connect.",
      "columns": {
        "id": { "type": "uuid", "primary_key": true },

        "cleaner_id": {
          "type": "uuid",
          "references": "cleaners.id",
          "nullable": false
        },

        "amount_cents": { "type": "bigint", "nullable": false },
        "currency": { "type": "text", "default": "usd", "nullable": false },

        "status": {
          "type": "payout_status_enum",
          "default": "pending",
          "nullable": false
        },
        "stripe_payout_id": { "type": "text" },
        "stripe_transfer_group": { "type": "text" },

        "period_start": { "type": "date" },
        "period_end": { "type": "date" },

        "attempt_count": { "type": "integer", "default": 0 },
        "failure_reason": { "type": "text" },
        "metadata": { "type": "jsonb" },

        "created_at": { "type": "timestamptz", "default": "NOW()" },
        "updated_at": { "type": "timestamptz", "default": "NOW()" },
        "paid_at": { "type": "timestamptz" }
      },
      "indexes": [
        "cleaner_id",
        "status",
        "period_start,period_end",
        "stripe_payout_id"
      ]
    }
  }

🧱 CHUNK 4 — SQL
Creates / aligns:

job_status_enum

job_event_type_enum

jobs table (adds missing columns if table already exists)

job_events table

👉 Copy–paste ALL of this into Neon SQL Editor (production branch) and run once.

--
-- ENUMS
--

DO $$ BEGIN
    CREATE TYPE job_status_enum AS ENUM (
        'draft',
        'scheduled',
        'in_progress',
        'completed',
        'cancelled_by_client',
        'cancelled_by_cleaner',
        'no_show_by_client',
        'no_show_by_cleaner'
    );
EXCEPTION
    WHEN duplicate_object THEN null;
END $$;

DO $$ BEGIN
    CREATE TYPE job_event_type_enum AS ENUM (
        'job_created',
        'client_updated',
        'cleaner_assigned',
        'cleaner_unassigned',
        'job_started',
        'job_completed',
        'client_approved',
        'client_disputed',
        'job_cancelled_client',
        'job_cancelled_cleaner',
        'auto_cancelled',
        'payment_released',
        'payment_refunded'
    );
EXCEPTION
    WHEN duplicate_object THEN null;
END $$;


--
-- JOBS TABLE
-- We create it if missing, and add any important columns if it already exists.
--

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS jobs (
    id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid()
);

-- Core relationships
ALTER TABLE jobs
    ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS client_id  UUID REFERENCES clients(id),
    ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS cleaner_id UUID REFERENCES cleaners(id);

-- Status & lifecycle
ALTER TABLE jobs
    ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS status           job_status_enum NOT NULL DEFAULT 'draft',
    ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS created_at       TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW(),
    ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS updated_at       TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW(),
    ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS cancelled_at     TIMESTAMPTZ;

-- Scheduling & timing
ALTER TABLE jobs
    ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS scheduled_start_at    TIMESTAMPTZ,
    ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS scheduled_end_at      TIMESTAMPTZ,
    ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS actual_start_at       TIMESTAMPTZ,
    ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS actual_end_at         TIMESTAMPTZ;

-- Duration
ALTER TABLE jobs
    ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS estimated_minutes     INTEGER,
    ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS actual_minutes        INTEGER;

-- Pricing & credits
ALTER TABLE jobs
    ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS base_rate_cents       BIGINT,
    ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS extra_fees_cents      BIGINT,
    ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS discount_cents        BIGINT,
    ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS total_charge_cents    BIGINT,
    ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS credit_charge_credits NUMERIC(12,2);

-- Misc
ALTER TABLE jobs
    ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS title  TEXT,
    ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS notes  TEXT,
    ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS metadata JSONB;

-- Automatic updated_at on jobs
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION update_jobs_updated_at()
RETURNS TRIGGER AS $$
BEGIN
    NEW.updated_at = NOW();
    RETURN NEW;
END;
$$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;

DROP TRIGGER IF EXISTS tr_jobs_updated ON jobs;

CREATE TRIGGER tr_jobs_updated
    BEFORE UPDATE ON jobs
    FOR EACH ROW EXECUTE FUNCTION update_jobs_updated_at();

-- Indexes
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_jobs_client_id
    ON jobs(client_id);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_jobs_cleaner_id
    ON jobs(cleaner_id);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_jobs_status
    ON jobs(status);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_jobs_scheduled_start
    ON jobs(scheduled_start_at);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_jobs_created_at
    ON jobs(created_at);


--
-- JOB EVENTS
-- Append-only log of everything that happens to a job.
--

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS job_events (
    id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),

    job_id UUID NOT NULL REFERENCES jobs(id),

    event_type job_event_type_enum NOT NULL,

    actor_type TEXT,           -- 'client', 'cleaner', 'system', 'admin'
    actor_id   UUID,           -- nullable, depends on actor_type

    from_status job_status_enum,
    to_status   job_status_enum,

    metadata JSONB,
    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW()
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_job_events_job_id
    ON job_events(job_id);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_job_events_event_type
    ON job_events(event_type);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_job_events_created_at
    ON job_events(created_at);
✅ As usual, yellow “already exists, skipping” messages are fine.
If you see a red error, screenshot it and send it to me.

🧩 CHUNK 5 – KPIs & Backups
Tables: kpi_daily, backup_runs

5A. SQL (run this in Neon)
--
-- KPI DAILY TABLE
-- Used by workflow 11 – KPI & Reporting Aggregator
--

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS kpi_daily (
    id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),

    -- date these metrics apply to
    metric_date DATE NOT NULL UNIQUE,

    -- core money and credits
    total_credits_purchased NUMERIC(14,2) NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
    total_credits_used      NUMERIC(14,2) NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
    total_revenue_cents     BIGINT NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
    total_payouts_cents     BIGINT NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,

    -- volume
    jobs_created    INT NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
    jobs_completed  INT NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,

    -- growth
    new_clients     INT NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
    new_cleaners    INT NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,

    -- raw snapshot or extra metrics (optional)
    snapshot JSONB,

    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_kpi_daily_date
    ON kpi_daily(metric_date);


--
-- BACKUP RUNS TABLE
-- Used by workflow 12 – Daily Backup & Snapshot
--

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS backup_runs (
    id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),

    run_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
    status TEXT NOT NULL,          -- 'started', 'success', 'failed', etc.
    notes TEXT,
    metadata JSONB
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_backup_runs_run_at
    ON backup_runs(run_at);

🧩 CHUNK 6 – Payment Failures & Integration Events
Tables: payment_failures, integration_events
These are not strictly required for the basic 12 workflows, but they’re very useful for:

debugging Stripe issues

tracking webhook behavior

building admin tools later

6A. SQL (run in Neon)
--
-- PAYMENT FAILURES
-- Stores failed Stripe payment attempts (useful for debugging + support).
--

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS payment_failures (
    id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),

    client_id UUID REFERENCES clients(id),

    stripe_payment_intent_id TEXT,
    stripe_event_id TEXT,
    stripe_error_code TEXT,
    stripe_error_message TEXT,

    amount_cents BIGINT,
    currency TEXT,

    raw_event JSONB,
    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_payment_failures_client_id
    ON payment_failures(client_id);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_payment_failures_stripe_pi
    ON payment_failures(stripe_payment_intent_id);


--
-- INTEGRATION EVENTS
-- Generic log of important events from external systems (Stripe, Twilio, etc).
--

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS integration_events (
    id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),

    provider TEXT NOT NULL,             -- 'stripe', 'twilio', 'sendgrid', etc.
    event_type TEXT NOT NULL,           -- e.g. 'webhook_received', 'sms_sent'
    external_id TEXT,                   -- e.g. Stripe event id, Twilio SID

    status TEXT,                        -- 'success', 'failed', etc.
    error_message TEXT,

    payload JSONB,                      -- raw data
    related_client_id UUID REFERENCES clients(id),
    related_cleaner_id UUID REFERENCES cleaners(id),

    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_integration_events_provider
    ON integration_events(provider);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_integration_events_event_type
    ON integration_events(event_type);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_integration_events_created_at
    ON integration_events(created_at);

🧩 CHUNK 7 – Cleaner Reliability Engine Tables
Tables: cleaner_reliability_events, cleaner_reliability_scores

These are for when we hook up:

no-shows

late check-ins

client ratings

cancellations

into a single reliability score per cleaner.

7A. SQL (run in Neon)
--
-- CLEANER RELIABILITY EVENTS
-- One row per reliability-relevant event (no show, late, 5-star, etc.).
--

DO $$ BEGIN
    CREATE TYPE reliability_event_type_enum AS ENUM (
        'job_on_time',
        'job_late_start',
        'job_late_finish',
        'job_no_show',
        'job_cancelled_short_notice',
        'job_cancelled_long_notice',
        'client_5_star',
        'client_4_star',
        'client_3_star_or_less',
        'dispute_opened',
        'dispute_lost',
        'dispute_won',
        'manual_adjustment_up',
        'manual_adjustment_down'
    );
EXCEPTION
    WHEN duplicate_object THEN null;
END $$;

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS cleaner_reliability_events (
    id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),

    cleaner_id UUID NOT NULL REFERENCES cleaners(id),
    job_id UUID REFERENCES jobs(id),

    event_type reliability_event_type_enum NOT NULL,
    weight NUMERIC(6,2) NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,  -- positive or negative impact

    notes TEXT,
    metadata JSONB,

    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_cleaner_rel_events_cleaner
    ON cleaner_reliability_events(cleaner_id);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_cleaner_rel_events_job
    ON cleaner_reliability_events(job_id);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_cleaner_rel_events_type
    ON cleaner_reliability_events(event_type);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_cleaner_rel_events_created_at
    ON cleaner_reliability_events(created_at);


--
-- CLEANER RELIABILITY SCORES
-- Current computed reliability per cleaner.
--

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS cleaner_reliability_scores (
    cleaner_id UUID PRIMARY KEY REFERENCES cleaners(id),

    current_score NUMERIC(5,2) NOT NULL DEFAULT 100,
    last_recalculated_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),

    -- optional detail fields
    total_events INT NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
    last_event_at TIMESTAMPTZ
);

🧩 CHUNK 8 – Cleaner Availability
8A. SQL (run this in Neon)
--
-- ENUM for availability recurrence
--

DO $$ BEGIN
    CREATE TYPE availability_recurrence_enum AS ENUM (
        'one_time',      -- single date/time window
        'weekly'         -- repeats every week on specified day_of_week
    );
EXCEPTION
    WHEN duplicate_object THEN null;
END $$;


--
-- CLEANER AVAILABILITY (ONE-TIME AND RECURRING)
--

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS cleaner_availability (
    id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),

    cleaner_id UUID NOT NULL REFERENCES cleaners(id),

    recurrence_type availability_recurrence_enum NOT NULL DEFAULT 'one_time',

    -- For weekly recurrence
    day_of_week SMALLINT,   -- 0=Sunday, 1=Monday, ... 6=Saturday

    -- Time window (in cleaner's local timezone)
    start_time_local TIME,
    end_time_local TIME,
    timezone TEXT,          -- e.g. 'America/New_York'

    -- For one-time blocks, you can also use explicit date
    date DATE,

    is_blocked BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT FALSE,  -- true = cannot book in this window

    notes TEXT,
    metadata JSONB,

    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
    updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);

CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION update_cleaner_availability_updated_at()
RETURNS TRIGGER AS $$
BEGIN
    NEW.updated_at = NOW();
    RETURN NEW;
END;
$$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;

DROP TRIGGER IF EXISTS tr_cleaner_availability_updated ON cleaner_availability;

CREATE TRIGGER tr_cleaner_availability_updated
    BEFORE UPDATE ON cleaner_availability
    FOR EACH ROW EXECUTE FUNCTION update_cleaner_availability_updated_at();

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_cleaner_availability_cleaner
    ON cleaner_availability(cleaner_id);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_cleaner_availability_recurrence
    ON cleaner_availability(recurrence_type);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_cleaner_availability_date
    ON cleaner_availability(date);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_cleaner_availability_dow
    ON cleaner_availability(day_of_week);

🧩 CHUNK 9 – Messaging (Threads + Messages)
This lets you later add:

in-app chat

SMS or email synced to threads

a simple messenger between client and cleaner

9A. SQL (run in Neon)
--
-- MESSAGE PARTICIPANT TYPE ENUM
--

DO $$ BEGIN
    CREATE TYPE participant_type_enum AS ENUM (
        'client',
        'cleaner',
        'admin',
        'system'
    );
EXCEPTION
    WHEN duplicate_object THEN null;
END $$;


--
-- MESSAGE THREADS
-- A conversation grouping (e.g. per job, or client<->cleaner channel).
--

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS message_threads (
    id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),

    job_id UUID REFERENCES jobs(id),
    client_id UUID REFERENCES clients(id),
    cleaner_id UUID REFERENCES cleaners(id),

    subject TEXT,
    metadata JSONB,

    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
    updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);

CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION update_message_threads_updated_at()
RETURNS TRIGGER AS $$
BEGIN
    NEW.updated_at = NOW();
    RETURN NEW;
END;
$$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;

DROP TRIGGER IF EXISTS tr_message_threads_updated ON message_threads;

CREATE TRIGGER tr_message_threads_updated
    BEFORE UPDATE ON message_threads
    FOR EACH ROW EXECUTE FUNCTION update_message_threads_updated_at();

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_message_threads_job
    ON message_threads(job_id);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_message_threads_client
    ON message_threads(client_id);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_message_threads_cleaner
    ON message_threads(cleaner_id);


--
-- MESSAGES
-- Individual messages in a thread.
--

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS messages (
    id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),

    thread_id UUID NOT NULL REFERENCES message_threads(id) ON DELETE CASCADE,

    sender_type participant_type_enum NOT NULL,
    sender_id UUID,

    body TEXT NOT NULL,
    sent_via TEXT,              -- 'in_app', 'sms', 'email', etc.
    external_id TEXT,           -- e.g. Twilio SID, email message ID

    is_read BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT FALSE,
    read_at TIMESTAMPTZ,

    metadata JSONB,

    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_messages_thread
    ON messages(thread_id);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_messages_sender
    ON messages(sender_type, sender_id);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_messages_created_at
    ON messages(created_at);
9B. JSON (save for n8n AI / docs)
{
  "enums": {
    "participant_type_enum": [
      "client",
      "cleaner",
      "admin",
      "system"
    ]
  },
  "tables": {
    "message_threads": {
      "description": "Conversation container, usually per job, between a client and cleaner.",
      "columns": {
        "id": { "type": "uuid", "primary_key": true },

        "job_id": { "type": "uuid", "references": "jobs.id" },
        "client_id": { "type": "uuid", "references": "clients.id" },
        "cleaner_id": { "type": "uuid", "references": "cleaners.id" },

        "subject": { "type": "text" },
        "metadata": { "type": "jsonb" },

        "created_at": { "type": "timestamptz", "default": "NOW()" },
        "updated_at": { "type": "timestamptz", "default": "NOW()" }
      },
      "indexes": [
        "job_id",
        "client_id",
        "cleaner_id"
      ]
    },
    "messages": {
      "description": "Individual messages in a thread, sent by clients, cleaners, admins, or the system.",
      "columns": {
        "id": { "type": "uuid", "primary_key": true },

        "thread_id": {
          "type": "uuid",
          "references": "message_threads.id",
          "nullable": false
        },

        "sender_type": {
          "type": "participant_type_enum",
          "nullable": false
        },

        "body": { "type": "text", "nullable": false },
        "sent_via": { "type": "text", "description": "in_app | sms | email | etc." },
        "external_id": { "type": "text" },

        "is_read": { "type": "boolean", "default": false },
        "read_at": { "type": "timestamptz" },

        "metadata": { "type": "jsonb" },
        "created_at": { "type": "timestamptz", "default": "NOW()" }
      },
      "indexes": [
        "thread_id",
        "sender_type,sender_id",
        "created_at"
      ]
    }
  }
}
🧩 CHUNK 10 – Admin & Audit Logs
These help with:

tracking what admins do

seeing which jobs were edited

future compliance / debugging

10A. SQL (run in Neon)
--
-- ADMIN USERS
-- Simple table for admin accounts (can expand later).
--

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS admin_users (
    id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),

    email TEXT NOT NULL UNIQUE,
    full_name TEXT,
    password_hash TEXT,         -- if you ever do admin login directly
    role TEXT,                  -- 'owner', 'support', 'ops', etc.

    is_active BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT TRUE,

    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
    updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);

CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION update_admin_users_updated_at()
RETURNS TRIGGER AS $$
BEGIN
    NEW.updated_at = NOW();
    RETURN NEW;
END;
$$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;

DROP TRIGGER IF EXISTS tr_admin_users_updated ON admin_users;

CREATE TRIGGER tr_admin_users_updated
    BEFORE UPDATE ON admin_users
    FOR EACH ROW EXECUTE FUNCTION update_admin_users_updated_at();

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_admin_users_email
    ON admin_users(email);


--
-- AUDIT LOG
-- Tracks important actions done by admins or by the system.
--

DO $$ BEGIN
    CREATE TYPE audit_actor_type_enum AS ENUM (
        'admin',
        'system'
    );
EXCEPTION
    WHEN duplicate_object THEN null;
END $$;

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS audit_log (
    id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),

    actor_type audit_actor_type_enum NOT NULL,
    actor_id UUID,                    -- references admin_users(id) when actor_type='admin'

    action TEXT NOT NULL,             -- e.g. 'update_job_status', 'manual_credit_adjustment'
    target_table TEXT,                -- e.g. 'jobs', 'clients'
    target_id UUID,                   -- row id affected

    details JSONB,                    -- what changed
    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_audit_log_actor
    ON audit_log(actor_type, actor_id);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_audit_log_target
    ON audit_log(target_table, target_id);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_audit_log_created_at
    ON audit_log(created_at);
10B. JSON (save for n8n AI)

      "columns": {

🧩 CHUNK 11 – Notifications (Templates + Log)
This will support things like:

“Credit purchase confirmation”

“Cleaner payout paid”

“Job reminder”

And logging EVERYTHING you send (for support / debugging)

11A. SQL (run in Neon)
--
-- ENUM for notification channels & status
--

DO $$ BEGIN
    CREATE TYPE notification_channel_enum AS ENUM (
        'email',
        'sms',
        'push',
        'in_app'
    );
EXCEPTION
    WHEN duplicate_object THEN null;
END $$;

DO $$ BEGIN
    CREATE TYPE notification_status_enum AS ENUM (
        'queued',
        'sent',
        'failed'
    );
EXCEPTION
    WHEN duplicate_object THEN null;
END $$;


--
-- NOTIFICATION TEMPLATES
-- Optional library of templates you can reference in workflows.
--

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS notification_templates (
    id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),

    template_key TEXT NOT NULL UNIQUE,         -- e.g. 'credit_purchase_receipt'
    channel notification_channel_enum NOT NULL,

    subject TEXT,                              -- for email / push
    body TEXT NOT NULL,                        -- can store handlebars-like template text
    is_active BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT TRUE,

    metadata JSONB,

    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
    updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);

CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION update_notification_templates_updated_at()
RETURNS TRIGGER AS $$
BEGIN
    NEW.updated_at = NOW();
    RETURN NEW;
END;
$$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;

DROP TRIGGER IF EXISTS tr_notification_templates_updated ON notification_templates;

CREATE TRIGGER tr_notification_templates_updated
    BEFORE UPDATE ON notification_templates
    FOR EACH ROW EXECUTE FUNCTION update_notification_templates_updated_at();



--
-- NOTIFICATION LOG
-- Every notification sent by the system (or attempted).
--

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS notification_log (
    id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),

    template_key TEXT,                         -- link to notification_templates.template_key (optional)
    channel notification_channel_enum NOT NULL,

    to_email TEXT,
    to_phone TEXT,
    to_push_token TEXT,

    subject TEXT,
    body TEXT,

    status notification_status_enum NOT NULL DEFAULT 'queued',
    error_message TEXT,

    related_client_id UUID REFERENCES clients(id),
    related_cleaner_id UUID REFERENCES cleaners(id),
    related_job_id UUID REFERENCES jobs(id),
    related_payment_id UUID REFERENCES payments(id),

    metadata JSONB,

    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
    sent_at TIMESTAMPTZ
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_notification_log_channel
    ON notification_log(channel);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_notification_log_status
    ON notification_log(status);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_notification_log_client
    ON notification_log(related_client_id);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_notification_log_cleaner
    ON notification_log(related_cleaner_id);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_notification_log_job
    ON notification_log(related_job_id);

🧩 CHUNK 12 – System Settings & Feature Flags
This gives you:

a system_settings table for key/value config (e.g. "credits_per_dollar")

a feature_flags table to turn features on/off without code

Super nice for future tweaks.

12A. SQL (run in Neon)
--
-- SYSTEM SETTINGS
-- Simple key/value config for the platform.
--

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS system_settings (
    key TEXT PRIMARY KEY,           -- e.g. 'credits_per_dollar', 'default_job_duration_minutes'
    value TEXT NOT NULL,            -- store as text, cast as needed in app
    description TEXT,
    updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);

CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION update_system_settings_updated_at()
RETURNS TRIGGER AS $$
BEGIN
    NEW.updated_at = NOW();
    RETURN NEW;
END;
$$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;

DROP TRIGGER IF EXISTS tr_system_settings_updated ON system_settings;

CREATE TRIGGER tr_system_settings_updated
    BEFORE UPDATE ON system_settings
    FOR EACH ROW EXECUTE FUNCTION update_system_settings_updated_at();


--
-- FEATURE FLAGS
-- Toggle features & experiments on/off without code changes.
--

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS feature_flags (
    key TEXT PRIMARY KEY,           -- e.g. 'enable_new_booking_flow'
    description TEXT,
    enabled BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT FALSE,
    rollout_percentage INT,         -- optional: 0–100 for gradual rollout
    metadata JSONB,

    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
    updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);

CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION update_feature_flags_updated_at()
RETURNS TRIGGER AS $$
BEGIN
    NEW.updated_at = NOW();
    RETURN NEW;
END;
$$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;

DROP TRIGGER IF EXISTS tr_feature_flags_updated ON feature_flags;

CREATE TRIGGER tr_feature_flags_updated
    BEFORE UPDATE ON feature_flags
    FOR EACH ROW EXECUTE FUNCTION update_feature_flags_updated_at();
12B. JSON (save for n8n AI / docs)

Think of this as 4 separate “boss checklists.”

🧾 1) STRIPE – EVERYTHING YOU NEED
1.1 Create & Configure the Stripe Account
What it is
Your Stripe account is the money brain: where card payments, refunds, disputes, and payouts live.

What you need

A main Stripe account (business details, bank account).

Business settings completed (legal entity, support email, branding).

How to complete

Log into Stripe → Settings → Business settings.

Fill:

Business name, address, support email, support URL.

Statement descriptor (e.g. “PURETASK*HOME CLEAN”).

Add your bank account under Payout settings.

1.2 Enable Needed Payment Methods
What it is
Card payments are default, but you may also want Apple Pay, Google Pay, etc.

What you need

Card payments enabled.

Optionally: wallet payments.

How to complete

Stripe Dashboard → Settings → Payment methods.

Enable:

Cards

Apple Pay / Google Pay (optional, but nice).

Make sure they are available for your country + currency (USD).

1.3 API Keys (Test + Live)
What it is
Keys you’ll use in Base44 and n8n to talk to Stripe.

What you need

Test secret key

Test publishable key

Live secret key

Live publishable key

How to complete

Stripe → Developers → API Keys.

For now:

Copy Test secret key and Test publishable key.

Store them in:

Base44 app config (secret)

n8n credentials (Stripe node)

Later, when going live:

Switch to Live mode in Stripe.

Grab Live keys and update Base44 + n8n.

1.4 Stripe Connect (for Cleaner Payouts)
What it is
Stripe Connect lets you pay cleaners (as “connected accounts”).

What you need

Choose Connect type (likely “Standard”).

Enable payouts to connected accounts.

A plan for how cleaners onboard (Stripe-hosted onboarding vs embedded).

How to complete

Stripe → Settings → Connect:

Enable Connect.

Choose Standard accounts (Stripe handles more compliance).

In your app / Base44:

Implement “Connect Stripe Account” for cleaners:

This opens a Stripe onboarding link.

Store the stripe_account_id in your cleaners table (we already have a column for that).

In Stripe:

Make sure payouts are enabled and your platform account is verified.

1.5 Webhooks (Core for n8n Workflows 01–09)
What it is
Stripe webhooks tell n8n when things happen (payments, refunds, disputes, payouts).

What you need

One webhook endpoint in Stripe pointing to n8n:

URL: https://<your-n8n-domain>/webhook/stripe/webhook

Events:

payment_intent.succeeded

payment_intent.payment_failed

charge.refunded

charge.dispute.created

charge.dispute.closed

payout.paid

payout.failed

How to complete

In n8n, confirm Workflow 01 – Stripe Webhook Ingest:

Has Webhook node at path: stripe/webhook.

In Stripe:

Go to Developers → Webhooks → “Add endpoint”.

Endpoint: your n8n URL + /webhook/stripe/webhook

Select the events above.

Save.

Copy the Webhook Signing Secret from Stripe.

Later you can validate signatures in n8n (optional for v1).

1.6 Payments for Credits (Credit Purchase Flow)
What it is
This is how clients buy credits. Stripe payment → n8n → Neon.

What you need

A frontend flow that creates a PaymentIntent (through Base44 or directly).

Workflow 03 aligned with the DB.

How to complete (high-level)

Frontend/Base44:

Use Stripe (or Base44’s Stripe-integrated flow) to create a PaymentIntent.

Attach metadata.client_id and any other needed info.

Stripe:

PaymentIntent → succeeded.

n8n Workflow 03 (must be updated):

On payment_intent.succeeded:

Upsert into payments table.

Insert into credit_transactions (type = 'purchase').

Update clients.credit_balance.

We’ll write the exact SQL when we focus on workflow 03.

1.7 Refunds & Disputes
What it is
Refund = voluntary return of money.
Dispute = chargeback initiated by the cardholder.

What you need

Policy: “All refunds are in credits” (we already decided).

Workflows:

05 – Refund Processor

06 – Dispute Opened

07 – Dispute Closed

How to complete

Refunds:

If you refund in Stripe (full or partial), Stripe fires charge.refunded.

Workflow 05 should:

Update payments.status.

Insert a negative credit transaction.

Adjust clients.credit_balance.

Disputes:

Stripe sends charge.dispute.created and charge.dispute.closed.

Workflow 06:

Insert row in disputes (status open).

Workflow 07:

Update disputes.status to won or lost.

Optionally write a cleaner_reliability_events entry.

1.8 Payouts (Transfers to Cleaners)
What it is
Stripe Connect payouts → actual bank transfers to cleaners.

What you need

A process to:

Calculate what each cleaner should earn (n8n/Neon).

Create a payout/transfer via Stripe.

Track it in Neon.

How to complete

Generate payout rows in payouts table for each cleaner (via n8n or Base44).

Use Stripe API (from n8n or Base44) to:

Create a transfer or payout to the connected account.

Stripe fires payout.paid / payout.failed.

08 → set payouts.status = 'paid', set paid_at.

09 → set payouts.status = 'failed', store failure_reason.

1.9 Test vs Live Mode
What it is
Two separate worlds in Stripe.

What you need

Test environment fully working before live.

A clean switch-over plan.

How to complete

Keep n8n + Base44 + frontend pointed at test keys until:

Payments, refunds, disputes, payouts all work end-to-end in test.

Before launch:

Duplicate config for live mode (webhooks, keys).

Update environment:

Base44 env: use live keys.

n8n Stripe credential: use live key.

Stripe webhooks: set live endpoint.

3.3 The 12 Workflows – Finalization
You already have all 12 set up; now each must be aligned.

For each:

01 – Stripe Webhook Ingest

Webhook node at /stripe/webhook.

Calls workflow 02 via Execute Workflow.

02 – Stripe Event Router

Trigger: “When executed by another workflow”.

Function node: Normalize Event.

Switch node by event_type.

Executes workflows 03–09.

03 – Payment Intent Succeeded Processor

Extract PI → write to payments, credit_transactions, update clients.

04 – Payment Intent Failed Processor

Write to payment_failures, update payments.status.

05 – Refund Processor

Updates payments and credit_transactions appropriately.

Adjusts clients.credit_balance.

06 – Dispute Opened Processor

Inserts into disputes.

07 – Dispute Closed Processor

Updates disputes.status, maybe reliability events.

08 – Payout Paid Processor

Updates payouts.status, paid_at.

09 – Payout Failed Processor

Updates payouts.status, failure_reason.

10 – Job Lifecycle Orchestrator

Receives job events from Base44/app.

Updates jobs, writes to job_events.

11 – KPI & Reporting Aggregator

Daily/cron.

Aggregates metrics into kpi_daily.

12 – Daily Backup & Snapshot

Logs to backup_runs.

Optionally triggers Neon backup/S3 export.

How to complete

We’ll go one-by-one (starting with 03) and:

Open the workflow in n8n.

Adjust SQL nodes to match the new Neon schema.

Test each workflow with sample payloads (from Stripe / Base44).

If a Stripe event or job event fails, log it + notify you.

Optionally send Slack/email to you.

Log backup_runs.

If something is off:

Fix workflows or add correction scripts.

✔ It's something you run once, not part of production logic

1. “DB Schema Installer”

Friendly, readable, non-technical.

If you want it grouped with other admin workflows later.

If you later add devops tasks to n8n.

“My Workflow 3”

“SQL Runner”

“Migration”

“Test Workflow”

“DB tools”

“TEMP SQL”

These cause problems later when you:

work with other engineers

revisit the app months later

build new schema updates

do production database changes

Clean structured naming now = no regrets later.
